2026-03-16T17:27:47.0606059Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0607010Z copilot: Now I understand the `m_nTempActionTime` field - from the plugin-sdk header:
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0607752Z ```
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0608047Z char                 m_nTempAction;
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0608494Z unsigned int         m_nTempActionTime;
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0608921Z ```
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0609071Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0611067Z `m_nTempActionTime` is NOT "when this tempAction was set". Looking at the log, the values are like 681025ms, 685050ms, etc. These values are close to `CTimer::m_snTimeInMilliseconds` at the time. So `elapsedMs = nowMs - m_nTempActionTime` gives huge values because `m_nTempActionTime` is NOT tracking when the current action was started.
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0613138Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0613144Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0618738Z Looking at the gta-reversed code, `m_nTempActionTime` actually stores the expiration time for the temp action—when it should end. The engine sets it by adding the duration to the current time, so `m_nTempActionTime = CTimer::m_snTimeInMilliseconds + duration`. This means if I want to know how much time remains, I should calculate `remainingMs = m_nTempActionTime - nowMs` instead of subtracting the other way around.
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0621289Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0632452Z The log is showing something odd though. On frame 813, the tempAction changes to HEADON_COLLISION with `tempActionElapsed = 681025ms`, but if that's the time *remaining* until expiration, it doesn't make sense for it to be that large right after the action is set. I'm wondering if `nowMs` is actually much smaller than `m_nTempActionTime`, or if the calculation is inverted from what I'm thinking. Let me work backwards from the frame number—if we're at frame 3250 running at ~60fps, that gives me a rough timestamp to compare against. So `m_nTempActionTime` stores the expiry timestamp—when the tempAction should expire—calculated as `CTimer::m_snTimeInMilliseconds + duration`. The engine clears the action when current time exceeds this value. Given the log shows 681025ms for a freshly-set collision action, that's way too high for a typical duration, which suggests `m_snTimeInMilliseconds` itself is already quite large—the game had been running long before this logging session started, so the absolute game time is much higher than the frame count alone would suggest. So the root cause is that `m_nTempActionTime` starts at 0 as a default, and when the code calculates elapsed time as `nowMs - 0`, it gets the full game session duration instead of recognizing that the action was never actually set. This causes the byTime condition to trigger immediately on the first frame, which is the bug. The fix would need to distinguish between "never set" (0) and "actually set to 0 game time."
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0641996Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0643716Z Looking deeper at what `m_nTempActionTime` represents in the plugin-sdk context, it seems like it's meant to store the expiration time in game milliseconds rather than when the action was set, so the engine can check if the current time has exceeded that threshold to automatically cancel the temp action.
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0645687Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0655846Z The frame-based detection is clearly working reliably across the log entries, while the time-based approach keeps producing false positives because `m_nTempActionTime` defaults to 0 and doesn't actually track when the action started—it's either already expired or never properly initialized, making elapsed time calculations meaningless. The real issue is that `m_nTempActionTime` is likely storing the remaining duration in milliseconds rather than an absolute timestamp, so when it's 0, the action expires immediately on the first frame. I need to reconsider what this field actually represents — if it's a countdown timer that the engine should be updating, then 0 would mean the action should terminate right away, which explains why the time-based detection fires instantly instead of waiting for the 500ms threshold. the observed behavior in the log. When `tempAction` switches from NONE to HEADON_COLLISION at frame 3250, `m_nTempActionTime` should reflect what the engine just wrote. Looking at the data: at that frame, `m_nTempActionTime` reads as 681025ms while `CTimer::m_snTimeInMilliseconds` is around 681033ms, which means the elapsed time calculation `taNow - taSet = 681025` implies `taSet ≈ 8ms` — but that math still doesn't check out.
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0664623Z 
2026-03-16T17:27:47.0669714Z Let me reconsider the formula: if `tempActionElapsed = taNow - taSet` and we're seeing 681025ms elapsed with `taNow ≈ 681033ms`, then `taSet` would need to be 8ms, which doesn't make sense. But if `taSet` is actually 0 (never initialized), then `taNow = 681025ms`, meaning the game time is about 11 minutes 21 seconds from start. For the REVERSE action at frame 3478, the elapsed time is 685050ms with `m_nTempActionTime` also at 0, giving the same result: `elapsed = 685050 - 0 = 685050ms`. So it appears `m_nTempActionTime` is initialized to 0 for both actions.

2026-03-16T17:29:00.4382936Z ### What This Means:
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4383061Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4383363Z - **`m_nTempActionTime = CTimer::GetTimeInMS() + durMs`** means:
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4383768Z   - Takes the current absolute game time (in milliseconds)
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4384094Z   - Adds the duration parameter
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4384380Z   - Result = the absolute game time when action expires
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4384664Z   
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4384845Z - **Example calls from CarAI.cpp:**
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4385092Z   ```cpp

2026-03-16T17:29:00.4386287Z   ```
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4386380Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4386659Z ### Important Issue Found:
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4386823Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4387666Z **m_nTempActionTime is NEVER actually checked in the current codebase.** No code compares it against `CTimer::GetTimeInMS()` to detect timeout. This appears to be a partially implemented feature where the infrastructure exists but the timeout logic is incomplete.

2026-03-16T17:29:00.4480160Z

2026-03-16T17:29:00.4493003Z     ### What This Means:
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4493204Z     
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4493463Z     - **`m_nTempActionTime = CTimer::GetTimeInMS() + durMs`** means:
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4493863Z       - Takes the current absolute game time (in milliseconds)
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4494186Z       - Adds the duration parameter
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4494490Z       - Result = the absolute game time when action expires
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4494779Z       
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4494974Z     - **Example calls from CarAI.cpp:**
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4495225Z       ```cpp
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4495545Z       vehAP->SetTempAction(TEMPACT_WAIT, 2'000);    // Set to expire 2000ms from now
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4496058Z       ap->SetTempAction(TEMPACT_REVERSE, 800);       // Set to expire 800ms from now
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4496628Z       ```
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4496896Z     
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4497078Z     ### Important Issue Found:
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4497300Z     
2026-03-16T17:29:00.4498233Z     **m_nTempActionTime is NEVER actually checked in the current codebase.** No code compares it against `CTimer::GetTimeInMS()` to detect timeout. This appears to be a partially implemented feature where the infrastructure exists but the timeout logic is incomplete.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3741420Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3742281Z copilot: Now let me read the actual drive code and config to fully understand the issues:
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3745883Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3746328Z copilot: Now I understand the problem with `m_nTempActionTime`:
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3747405Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3747591Z From the gta-reversed code:
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3747974Z ```cpp
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3748533Z void CAutoPilot::SetTempAction(eAutoPilotTempAction action, uint32 durMs) {
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3749219Z     m_nTempAction = action;
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3750416Z     m_nTempActionTime = CTimer::GetTimeInMS() + durMs;  // ← expiry time, NOT set time
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3751135Z }
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3751397Z ```
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3751546Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3752026Z So `m_nTempActionTime` = `CTimer::GetTimeInMS() + durMs` = EXPIRY TIME (when the action should stop).
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3752687Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3752693Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3754667Z This means my calculation is inverted—when I subtract the expiry time from now, I get a negative value that wraps around to a huge unsigned number if the action is still running, but becomes positive once it's expired. To get the actual elapsed time, I need to flip the subtraction around.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3756670Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3759243Z Looking at the actual code calls, actions like `TEMPACT_WAIT` and `TEMPACT_REVERSE` have explicit durations in milliseconds, but `HEADON_COLLISION` doesn't expire on its own—it persists until the obstacle clears. Since I don't have the duration stored for that case, I can't reliably calculate how long it's been active.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3761338Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3762931Z The real clue is in the log: the elapsed time shows 681025ms, which is way too small to be an unsigned integer wraparound (that would be ~4 billion ms). This suggests `m_nTempActionTime` was never actually set when `HEADON_COLLISION` triggered, or it's still zero from initialization.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3764561Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3767852Z Looking at the sequence, when action 19 first appears, the elapsed time equals the total game runtime (~681 seconds), which means `m_nTempActionTime` must be 0. This immediately satisfies the byTime condition since 681025ms exceeds the 500ms threshold. Then at frame 3477, when the action changes back to NONE, the elapsed time is only 8ms—suggesting `m_nTempActionTime` was finally set at that point, possibly when the engine cleared the action.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3770603Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3775901Z The pattern is clear: the engine directly assigns certain actions like HEADON_COLLISION and REVERSE without calling SetTempAction(), so `m_nTempActionTime` never gets updated for these cases. This means the time-based detection is fundamentally broken for these actions—it fires immediately based on stale or zero values rather than actual elapsed time. The frame-counting approach was the reliable method all along, and adding time-based detection was a mistake that needs to be reverted.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3779218Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3781579Z But stepping back, the user's actual complaints are about the recruit turning the wrong way at intersections and crashing when swerving—those are the real problems to solve. The HEADON_PERSISTENT timing issue is secondary. Let me dig into the intersection logs to understand what's causing the wrong direction turns.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3783641Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3787511Z Looking at the WRONG_DIR events, I see the recruit's heading oscillating between roughly 0 and -0.07 (pointing North) while the target heading flips between +1.559 and -1.582 (East-West directions). This is clearly an intersection where the road segment runs East-West but the player went straight North, and our custom lane alignment code is picking the road-node heading instead of the autopilot link heading, leaving the recruit confused about which direction to follow. The oscillation happens because the recruit keeps switching between these conflicting headings.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3791065Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3792998Z The real problem is that every time WRONG_DIR_RECOVER triggers and resets the mission to MC52, it causes the autopilot to potentially pick a different road segment, which perpetuates the cycle. I need to look at how the WRONG_DIR handling and ApplyLaneAlignment code work to understand why we're getting this mismatch at intersections.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3795400Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3796075Z I'm also noticing REVERSE actions appearing in the logs, which suggests there's a separate swerving issue I need to investigate.
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3797150Z 
2026-03-16T17:29:53.3799724Z The core issue seems to be that at intersections, we're calculating the target heading from the road node instead of from the player's actual direction, so WRONG_DIR keeps triggering even though the recruit is correctly following the player through the intersection. The vanilla traffic AI handles this naturally with MC52 (FOLLOW mode), so I need to figure out why our detection is interfering with that.

2026-03-16T17:35:06.2009083Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2009610Z copilot: Now I have a very good understanding of the code. Let me diagnose the key issues:
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2010323Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2010578Z ## Issue 1: WRONG_DIR oscillation at intersections
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2010865Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2010963Z Looking at the log pattern:
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2011635Z - Frame 5288: `WRONG_DIR_START` heading=-0.074, targetH=-1.582, deltaH=-1.508 (just over 1.5 threshold)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2012727Z - Frame 5309: `WRONG_DIR_END` heading=0.062, targetH=1.559, deltaH=1.498 (just under 1.5 threshold)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2013530Z - Frame 5329: `WRONG_DIR_START` again
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2013853Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2013859Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2014022Z - Frame 5349: `WRONG_DIR_END` again
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2014501Z - Frame 5364: `WRONG_DIR_START` again
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2014807Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2017318Z The recruit's heading stays near 0 (North) while the target heading oscillates between roughly -1.582 (West) and +1.559 (East), causing the delta to flip back and forth across the 1.5 radian threshold. This is happening where the player stopped and the recruit is on an East-West road with nodes at ±1.57 radians.
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2019239Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2024113Z The issue is that `ApplyLaneAlignment` returns the road node heading, and the WRONG_DIR detection fires because the current heading (~0) versus the road heading (±1.57) gives a delta of about 1.57 radians, which exceeds the 1.5 threshold. At intersections, the vehicle heading naturally lags behind the road direction during turns, so this detection is too sensitive and triggers unnecessarily. Increasing the WRONG_DIR_THRESHOLD_RAD from 1.5 to 1.7 would give more breathing room at these junctures. So the recruit is heading north when it should be heading west — a 86-degree difference that's a genuine navigation error, not a backwards direction. The real issue seems to be that when the player stops at an intersection, the recruit gets confused about which road segment to follow and starts oscillating between heading options instead of committing to the correct path.
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2027747Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2029424Z The `ApplyLaneAlignment` function is flipping the target heading back and forth between west and east on alternating frames because of a `ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH` condition, which tanks the recruit's speed and triggers a recovery mission that breaks the autopilot's normal behavior. The underlying problem is that `GetNearestRoadHeading` picks a direction based on the current heading, but that heading keeps changing, so it can't settle on a consistent target.
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2031002Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2032456Z I'm considering two fixes: either suppress the WRONG_DIR recovery when the player is stopped and the recruit is nearby (letting it naturally reposition), or raise the threshold from 1.5 radians to something like 2.0 or 2.2 so that 90-degree misalignments at intersections don't trigger it. I notice there was a dynamic threshold approach in earlier code that used 2.3 radians for close-range situations, which might be worth revisiting.
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2033978Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2034764Z The core issue with the oscillating heading values seems to stem from the road-heading lookup flipping between opposite directions on consecutive frames, so I need to add hysteresis to stabilize that. heading calculation, or use a stable reference.
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2035647Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2036135Z Actually looking more carefully at the log: when the recruit is heading North (~0) and the road goes East-West, `GetNearestRoadHeading` calculates the heading as:
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2037206Z - `headingForward = atan2(dx, dy)` for the East direction ≈ +1.57 (East)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2037772Z - `headingBack = headingForward + π ≈ -1.57` (West)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2038104Z - Chooses the one closer to `currentHeading`
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2038438Z - `currentHeading` ≈ 0 (North)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2038710Z - `AbsHeadingDelta(+1.57, 0) = 1.57` (East)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2038993Z - `AbsHeadingDelta(-1.57, 0) = 1.57` (West)
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2039616Z - TIE! And the recruit's heading is oscillating slightly between slightly positive and slightly negative, so the tie-breaking flips each frame.
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2040139Z 
2026-03-16T17:35:06.2040957Z This is the root cause of the oscillation. When `currentHeading ≈ 0` (North) and the road is exactly East-West (±1.57 rad from North), the two directions are equidistant, and tiny fluctuations in heading cause them to flip.

2026-03-16T17:35:34.5705315Z   result: {"type":"text","text":{"value":"The system that controls car navigation and autopilot in GTA San Andreas relies on a network of road nodes and links—essentially a navigation graph embedded into the game world. This system is responsible for how traffic flows, how AI drivers choose their route, and how autopilot features (like taxi missions or NPC car journeys) behave.\n\n### Road Nodes, Links, and Navigation\n\n- **Nodes:** Points in 3D space that mark positions on roads, intersections, and other travelable surfaces.\n- **Links:** Connections between nodes that indicate valid paths a vehicle can follow. Each node typically connects to two or more neighboring nodes, forming a double-linked (undirected) graph for smooth travel in both directions.\n- **Path Data:** Stored in `nodes*.dat` files within `gta3.img`, split into 64 squares (750x750 units each) covering the map. This keeps memory usage efficient, only loading relevant areas as the player moves around【3:0†source】.\n\n### CCarPathLink and Orientation Alignment\n\nThe class `CCarPathLink` is part of the internal C++ code that controls how cars traverse these links. While direct, official documentation for each specific method (such as `ClipTargetOrientationToLink`) is rare, here's how it's typically understood:\n\n- **ClipTargetOrientationToLink:** This utility function ensures that when an automatic (AI) or scripted car navigates from one link (segment between two nodes) to another, its orientation (heading) aligns with the direction of the link. For example, a car turning from a northbound road to eastbound will have its orientation smoothly constrained (“clipped”) to match the actual road direction after the turn, preventing abrupt or physically impossible movements.\n- **Use in Navigation:** When the autopilot or AI drivers need to follow a path, they fetch the sequence of links between the current and target node, then adjust their steering and orientation using helper functions like `ClipTargetOrientationToLink` to ensure smooth, road-following motion rather than direct, unrealistic movement between arbitrary world coordinates.\n\n### Modding and Visualization\n\nModders and reverse engineers have deeply investigated these systems. For instance:\n- Tools like the [paths-visualizer Blender addon](https://github.com/Swoorup/paths-visualizer) allow importing/exporting and visualizing nodes and links from the game's binary path files, revealing how vehicles and pedestrians plot their courses【3:5†source】.\n- SDKs such as DK22Pac's plugin-sdk expose classes like `CCarPathLink` to C++ so modders can create new AI behaviors or navigation features【3:6†source】.\n\n### Practical Impact: GPS and Autopilot Mods\n\nCommunity GPS mods (like GTA GPS Redux) hook into these systems to offer real-time, in-game navigation. They:\n- Find the nearest node to a target/the player's car.\n- Run a shortest-path algorithm (like A*) over the road-node network.\n- Generate a list of links to follow, and guide the car or player icon using these nodes, using similar orientation correction logic to keep directions physically plausible【3:2†source】【3:4†source】.\n\n### Summary\n\n- **Road nodes and links** form the digital map for car navigation in GTA SA.\n- **CCarPathLink::ClipTargetOrientationToLink** (in C++-level code) corrects car headings, ensuring cars drive realistically by aligning their facing with the direction of the upcoming node/link.\n- This is fundamental for both built-in autopilot (AI traffic/cabs) and sophisticated community mods that create GPS and navigation features.\n\nFor code-level exploration, the [plugin-sdk](https://github.com/DK22Pac/plugin-sdk/blob/master/plugin_sa/game_sa/CCarPathLink.h) is the best source, and for path file structure, GTAMods has a detailed guide【3:0†source】【3:6†source】【3:5†source】.","annotations":[{"text":"【3:0†source】","start_index":933,"end_index":945,"url_citation":{"title":"Paths (GTA SA) - Each node includes:\n  - 3D position data (X, Y, Z coordinates)\n  - Link ID: index of its first outgoing link\n  - Area ID: indicates which of the 64 path sectors (each 750×750 units) the node belongs to\n  - Node ID: unique per-area, incremental number\n  - Path width, flags for node function (e.g., regular, highway, parking, emergency)【3:0†source】【3:2†source】【3:3†source】\n\n- **CCarPathLink** represents a connection (directed edge) between two nodes. Each link contains:\n  - Indices of the source and destination nodes\n  - Direction vector (compressed)\n  - Lane information: how many left/right lanes are available, and one-way/bi-directional flags\n\nThe entire city's path layout is stored in a grid of 64 NODES*.DAT files, each covering a square region. These are loaded dynamically for active areas of the map, ensuring efficient memory usage【3:0†source】【3:1†source】【3:4†source】.\n\n**Navigation & Intersection Handling**\n\n- The network forms a bidirectional graph, so most nodes have at least two links (to previous and next nodes on a road), but intersections will have three or more links enabling choice of direction【3:3†source】【3:9†source】.\n- Links are grouped for multi-lane roads using lane indexing, and nodes/links include flags indicating vehicle/pedestrian access, traffic direction, intersection status, and spawn rates (probability of an AI vehicle or pedestrian spawning at that point)【3:3†source】.\n\n**Car AI (NPC Driving Logic)**\n\n- Each AI car has a **CAutoPilot** component that keeps track of its current node, target node, lane, and planned path. The autopilot system:\n  - Requests a route between nodes using the node-link network (shortest path or preferred direction)\n  - Picks lanes, switching at intersections as allowed by the link data and traffic rules\n  - Smoothly interpolates position between nodes for curved and natural-looking turns\n- At intersections (nodes with 3+ links), the car's AI uses navigation tables, road rules, and sometimes randomization to choose an outbound link that matches its goal, while avoiding illegal turns (as flagged in the link/intersection data)\n- Special node/link flags mark traffic lights, forbidden turns, or unique behaviors (like boat-only or emergency-only paths), further guiding the car's choices【3:3†source】【3:9†source】.\n\n**Summary**\n\n1. 2026-03-16T17:37:00.6911315Z copilot: Now I have a clear picture. Let me also fetch the CPathFind.h and CNodeAddress from plugin-sdk:
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6912020Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6912450Z Actually, let me now focus on implementing the fixes. I have all the understanding I need.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6913083Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6913557Z Let me look at the full log to understand what ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH cases look like vs CLIPPED_LINK:
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6914189Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6914319Z From the log:
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6914930Z - `align=ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH` - our code chose road-node heading over clipped-link heading
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6915908Z - `align=CLIPPED_LINK` - used the autopilot's ClipTargetOrientationToLink result
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6916662Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6918164Z The CCarPathLink has `m_nDirX` and `m_nDirY` which are the compressed direction vector of the link. `ClipTargetOrientationToLink` uses this direction to set the target heading for the car. So `align=CLIPPED_LINK` gives the actual road direction for the current link.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6919869Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6919875Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6923019Z When we hit ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH, our heuristic is overriding the clipped direction because it's too far from both the road-node heading and the car's current heading. In the oscillating case from the logs, the clipped link direction is correct for the E-W road, but our road-node calculation keeps flipping between East and West while the car is actually heading North—both are wrong, so the mismatch override is triggering incorrectly.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6925708Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6930810Z The real problem is that ApplyLaneAlignment was built to refine heading estimates for WRONG_DIR detection and AdaptiveSpeed, but at intersections where the car is perpendicular to the road, all our heading estimates become unreliable and start oscillating. I'm realizing now that CCarPathLink actually gives us the true direction of the current road segment through its direction components, which is what the autopilot uses for navigation—when we see align=CLIPPED_LINK, that's the correct answer. The issue is that GetNearestRoadHeading uses two path nodes to compute a heading, and at intersections those two nearest nodes might not represent the actual road direction.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6935086Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6939884Z The oscillation happens because when the car is at an intersection heading North on an E-W road, the clipped link heading points West, which differs from North by more than our threshold, so we fall back to the road-node heading. But the two nearest nodes could give us either East or West, and since both are equally wrong from North, the choice flips back and forth based on tiny heading noise. The fix is to add hysteresis in ApplyLaneAlignment when we hit ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH—use the last known road heading as a tiebreaker in GetNearestRoadHeading to prevent oscillating between East and West when the car is exactly perpendicular to the road.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6943969Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6950443Z But I'm realizing the ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH condition might not even be triggering here. Let me trace through the math: when clipVsCurrent is 1.57 and roadVsCurrent is also 1.57, the condition checks if `roadVsCurrent + MARGIN < clipVsCurrent`, which becomes `1.77 < 1.57`—that's false, so ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH shouldn't activate at all. Yet the logs show it is, so either my understanding of which headings are being compared is off, or there's something else going on with how the road-node heading is being selected. I see the pattern now—ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH triggers when the road-node heading is significantly closer to the current car heading than the clipped link heading is, meaning the road-node gives better directional info than the current link. When the road-node oscillates between East and West while the car heads North, I need to trace through what happens in each case to understand why the alignment keeps switching.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6955831Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6958979Z Looking at the actual scenario: the autopilot link is pointing backward (South) while the car heads North, and the road-node heading alternates between East and West. Since both East and West are closer to North than South is, ROAD_NODE_MISMATCH keeps firing and picking whichever road-node heading is available that frame, causing the oscillation. Then WRONG_DIR triggers because the car heading differs from the oscillating road-node heading by about 1.57 radians, just above the threshold.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6961934Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6963158Z The fix is to add hysteresis to the road-node heading calculation so it doesn't flip-flop between East and West, and slightly raise the WRONG_DIR threshold from 1.5 to 1.6 radians to avoid false positives at 90-degree intersections.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6964472Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6967455Z I'm also considering whether the time-based logic in HEADON_PERSISTENT and REVERSE_STUCK is actually working correctly—the way `m_nTempActionTime` stores expiry time means the duration calculation is broken, so I should rely on the frame counter instead. Additionally, I should prevent the periodic road-snap when the recruit is close to the player with a valid link, and trigger a road-snap after exiting a swerve maneuver to recover the route.
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6969999Z 
2026-03-16T17:37:00.6970393Z Now I need to examine the ApplyLaneAlignment function and implement these changes.

`00h` (4 bytes, UINT32): Number of all nodes (Section 1 total: vehicle + ped)\n  - `04h` (4 bytes, UINT32): Number of vehicle nodes\n  - `08h` (4 bytes, UINT32): Number of pedestrian nodes\n  - `0Ch` (4 bytes, UINT32): Number of navi nodes\n  - `10h` (4 bytes, UINT32): Number of links (applies to path, navi, and link-related sections)\n\n### 2. **Section 1: Path Nodes**\n- Vehicle nodes come first, then pedestrian nodes.\n- **Node entry: 28 bytes, structure:**\n  - `00h` (4 bytes, UINT32): Pointer/Address – unused\n  - `04h` (4 bytes, UINT32): Always zero, unused\n  - `08h` (6 bytes, 3x INT16): Position (X, Y, Z)\n  - `0Eh` (2 bytes, INT16): Unknown (often `0x7FFE`)\n  - `10h` (2 bytes, UINT16): Link ID (index into Links section)\n  - `12h` (2 bytes, UINT16): Area ID (matches filename)\n  - `14h` (2 bytes, UINT16): Node ID (increases by 1, unique per file)\n  - `16h` (1 byte, UINT8): Path Width\n  - `17h` (1 byte, UINT8): Node Flags (see below)\n  - ...and possible padding / extras\n\nYou’ll find vehicle path nodes at the start, immediately followed by pedestrian path nodes (all use the same format for path entries).\n\n#### Vehicle Node Flags\n- Indicates behaviors (traffic lights, crossing allowed, speed, etc.). Full bitmask breakdown is on the wiki.\n\n### 3. **Section 2: Navi Nodes**\n- Additional navigation nodes for AI. Structure is similar to path nodes, but tailored for navigation/route-finding NPC features.\n\n### 4. **Section 3: Links**\n- Binary links that connect nodes: double-linked (undirected) graph.\n- Each entry:\n  - Source node index, target node index (for adjacency list)\n  - Plus route traversal data (direction, costs, etc.).\n\n### 5-7. **Further sections**\n- Navi links, filler, link lengths, intersection-specific flags, etc.\n\n### **Byte Offsets**\n- After header (20 bytes), first (vehicle) path node entry starts at 20h.\n- Total path node count: Header[0x04] + Header[0x08]\n- Path node section size: (total nodes) × 28 bytes\n- Followed by navi nodes (count from header).\n- Then the links, and so on.\n\n---\n\n## Practical Notes\n\n- Nodes files are **double-linked, undirected graphs** encoded in adjacency list form, permitting vehicle AI to traverse, plan, and \"see\" routes roughly as players do.\n- The game streams only those `nodes*.dat` files that cover/map the area surrounding the player.\n- Corrupt or mismatched files may cause the game to crash on entering an affected region【3:3†source】.\n\n---\n\n## **References & Further Documentation**\n\n- **GTAMods Wiki - Paths (GTA SA)**: The most comprehensive technical documentation, with full hex offsets, structure breakdown, field definitions, and links to community tools (also mirrored at open.mp and Grand Theft Wiki):\n  - [GTAMods Paths (GTA SA)](https://gtamods.com/wiki/Paths_(GTA_SA))【3:0†source】\n  - [Grand Theft Wiki - Paths (GTA SA)](https://www.grandtheftwiki.com/Paths_(GTA_SA))【3:1†source】\n  - [Open.mp Path Nodes archival version](https://www.open.mp/th/docs/scripting/resources/path-nodes)【3:2†source】\n- **Community Tools & Forums**:\n  - [GTAForums compiled node research thread](https://gtaforums.com/topic/214901-compiled-path-nodes/)【3:3†source】\n  - [SAMP Forums with decompilation tips](https://sampforum.blast.hk/showthread.php?tid=664614)【3:7†source】\n- **Node Editing Tools**:\n  - [SA Path Utility (SAPU)](https://zzpumazone.blogspot.com/2024/08/sa-path-utility-sapu-v10.html) – for merging, moving, and editing node files【3:8†source】\n  - [GTA DAT Toolkit Inspector & Converter](https://github.com/MadGamerHD/-GTA-DAT-Toolkit-Inspector-Chase-Nodes-Converter) – for converting/inspecting binary nodes data【3:5†source】\n\n---\n\n### **For Developers**\nIf you're writing a parser or reader:\n- Parse the header first (20 bytes, all UINT32).\n- Read/seek per section as indicated above.\n- If you want to process only vehicle nodes, count equals header[1].\n- Pay attention to all fields and consult the wiki table for bit-level flag definitions (traffic, route, intersection, etc.), as these can be important for traffic behavior in mods.\n\n---\n\n**Summary**: The detailed structure and byte offsets for GTA SA's nodes.dat vehicle path nodes are thoroughly documented, especially on GTAMods Wiki. You can parse these files by reading the 20-byte header then iterating through the 28-byte node records. 2026-03-16T17:44:59.2591690Z

2026-03-16T17:46:35.9253467Z copilot: Let me verify the Fix D block structure is correct (I added a `{` wrapper):
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9256800Z 
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9258432Z copilot: The `AdaptiveSpeed` function is using `WRONG_DIR_THRESHOLD_RAD` as the boundary between "curve" and "wrong direction". This is fine since it's for speed modulation, not for WRONG_DIR start/stop detection. The static 1.5 rad threshold here is actually appropriate because:
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9261546Z 1. If absDH > 1.5 rad in `AdaptiveSpeed`, the car IS going in the wrong direction in terms of speed — it should go slow
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9263918Z 2. If we use the close-range threshold (2.0 rad) here, we'd let the car go at full speed when absDH is 1.5-2.0 rad (which is 86°-115° — that's quite a large misalignment)
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9265107Z 
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9265471Z 
2026-03-16T17:46:35.9288248Z When the recruit is heading more than 86° away from the target, reducing speed to 30% is the right call regardless of distance. The `WRONG_DIR_THRESHOLD_CLOSE_RAD = 2.0 rad` only triggers the WRONG_DIR recovery mechanism, not the speed reduction itself. So the current `AdaptiveSpeed` logic with 1.5 rad is correct as-is. Now I need to verify the `ApplyLaneAlignment` function to ensure the threshold usage is consistent throughout, particularly in the road heading alignment checks.
